I need to compare each candidate against the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT:** `-0.0892421*v³ - 0.725306*v*(1 - x²) - 1.44736*x - 1.44736*x*exp(-|x|)`

Expanding: `-0.0892421*v³ - 0.725306*v + 0.725306*v*x² - 1.44736*x - 1.44736*x*exp(-|x|)`

The GT has these basis functions:
1. `v³` 
2. `v`
3. `v*x²`
4. `x`
5. `x*exp(-|x|)`

The key challenge is the term `x*exp(-|x|)`. This is NOT a polynomial, NOT `x*|x|`, and NOT expressible as a finite polynomial in x. Let me check each candidate.

**Key observations about `x*exp(-|x|)`:**
- Taylor series: `x*exp(-|x|) = x - x*|x| + x*|x|²/2 - ...` (infinite series)
- It cannot be exactly represented by any finite combination of polynomials, `x*|x|`, `log(...)`, etc.
- `x*exp(-|x|)` is an odd function (since `|(-x)| = |x|`, so `(-x)*exp(-|-x|) = -x*exp(-|x|)`)

Let me check candidates that might contain `exp` terms or could potentially match:

**Candidate 5:** `c0*x*exp(c1*x) + c2*v + c3*v*x² + c4*v*|v| + c5*x/(c6*x²+1)`
- Has `x*exp(c1*x)` but NOT `x*exp(-|x|)`. `exp(c1*x)` ≠ `exp(-|x|)` since |x| ≠ ±x for all x.
- Has `v*|v|` instead of `v³`. Note: `v*|v| = v²*sign(v)` ≠ `v³` (since `v³ = v*v²` and `v*|v| = |v|*v*sign(v)/|v|`... actually `v*|v| = |v|*v` while `v³ = v*v*v`. For v>0: `v*|v| = v²` and `v³ = v³`. These are different.)
- Missing `x` term as standalone. `x/(c6*x²+1)` ≠ `x` unless c6=0, giving `x/1 = x`. But then we'd need `x*exp(-|x|)` from `x*exp(c1*x)`, which requires `c1*x = -|x|`, impossible for all x.

Candidate 5 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 47:** `c0*x*exp(c1*x) + c2*v + c3*v*x² + c4*v*|v| + c5*x³`
- Same issue: `x*exp(c1*x)` ≠ `x*exp(-|x|)`, and `v*|v|` ≠ `v³`.

Candidate 47 verdict: [NO MATCH]

For all purely polynomial candidates (most candidates), they cannot produce `x*exp(-|x|)`. Let me quickly scan for any candidate that has `exp(-|x|)` or equivalent... None do.

Candidates with `x*|x|`: 1, 2, 10, 13, 19. Note `x*|x| = |x|*x = x²*sign(x)`, which is NOT equal to `x*exp(-|x|)`.

Candidates with `log(|x|+1)` terms: 2, 12, 13, 15, 16, 19, 42, 43, 44, 48. These can't produce `exp(-|x|)`.

Candidates with `exp(t)` or `cos(t)`: 6, 7, 23, 38-41, 48, 49, 50. Setting time-dependent coefficients to 0 removes those terms, leaving polynomial-like expressions that can't match.

**Every candidate** either lacks the `x*exp(-|x|)` term entirely or has `x*exp(c*x)` which cannot equal `x*exp(-|x|)` for both positive and negative x simultaneously.
